Amm and Khass — General and Specific
advanced
12 min
Delayed Takhsis of Qur'an by Solitary Hadith: A Hanafi-Shafi'i Dispute
Hanafi rebuttal of Shafi'i claim of delayed specification by solitary hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rejects delayed specification (takhsis) of a definitive (qat'i) text by a probable (zanni) text, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of this dispute.

Core Idea
Delayed specification of a definitive text by a probable text is not allowed in Hanafi usul; it would be abrogation, which is also impermissible.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the validity of delayed takhsis. The Shafi'is argue that a solitary hadith can specify a general Qur'anic verse even if the hadith came later. The Hanafis respond with three arguments, ultimately concluding that such a delayed specification is either simultaneous/preceding, based on another verse, or would constitute invalid abrogation. Understanding this debate clarifies the Hanafi principle that a qat'i text cannot be altered by a zanni one.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine the specific legal question being debated: whether a general Qur'anic verse (Anfal:41) can be specified by a solitary hadith ('من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه') that was narrated after the verse's revelation.
This is a dispute about delayed takhsis of a qat'i text by a zanni text.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its evidence
Summarize the Shafi'i argument: the hadith is a valid specifier regardless of timing because specification is allowed by any evidence, and the hadith is well-known (mashhur).
Shafi'is also hold that the killer automatically gets the spoil.
3
Analyze the first Hanafi argument: historical precedence
Examine the claim that the verse was revealed after the battle of Badr, while the hadith was already applied (e.g., giving the spoil of Abu Jahl to his killer). Thus the specification is simultaneous or preceding, not delayed.
If specification is simultaneous (muqaran) or preceding (muqaddam), it is valid and does not raise the issue of delayed takhsis.
4
Analyze the second Hanafi argument: alternative specifier from another verse
Consider the proposition that the real specifier is Qur'an verse 65 of Surah al-Anfal ('Urge the believers to fight'), which is an absolute command that includes giving spoil as an incentive. This is a qat'i text, so it can specify the other qat'i text.
This argument avoids the need for a zanni specifier entirely.
5
Analyze the third Hanafi argument: delayed = abrogation
Understand the logical consequence: if the hadith is indeed delayed and specifies the verse, it effectively abrogates part of the general rule. But abrogation of the Qur'an by a solitary hadith is impermissible in Hanafi usul. Therefore, delayed takhsis is essentially naskh, which is also prohibited.
Some objections to this argument are raised and answered in the passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أنه صارفة وهو خلاف ضروريات العربية وأيضاً لا نعتقد بعقد ولا فسخ ولا بصدق ولا كذب، فإنه يجوز أن يكون مجازاً تظهر القرينة بعده، أو مخصوصاً يظهر مخصصه بعده، وهذا القول بالقطعية أظهر فتدبر الشافعية قالوا :أولاً: جعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم (السلب للقاتل مطلقاً أذن به الإمام أم لا كما هو قول الشافعي وأحمد أو برأي الإمام فقط (كما هو قول الإمام أبي حنيفة ومالك بعد (قوله تعالى: ﴿وَاعْلَمُوا أَنَّمَا غَنِمْتُم مِّن شَيْءٍ فَأَنَّ للَّهِ مُمَسَهُ وَلِلرَّسُولِ ﴾ [الأنفال: ٤١] (الآية) وكان عاماً موجباً لإيجاب الخمس من السلب (فقد خص السلب (عنه) (متراخياً قالوا المخصص قوله عليه وآله وأصحابه الصلاة والسلام: «من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه» رواه الشيخان وحمله الإمامان الشافعي وأحمد على التشريع العام، فجعلا القاتل مستحقاً له، والإمامان أبو حنيفة ومالك قالا : كان هذا إذناً منه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم لكونه إماماً، فلا يفيد استحقاق القاتل مطلقاً، وهذا هو الأصوب، ويؤيده عليه الصلاة والسلام لما أمر خالد بن الوليد رضي الله عنه فلم يعط السلب للقاتل فشكي إليه الله فسأله فقال انا استكثرناه يا رسول الله فقال ذلك القاتل لخالد كلمة، فغضب عليه رسول الله له ولو لم يعنف خالداً ولم ينكره وهو مذكور في صحيح مسلم وسنن أبي داود (قلنا) :أولاً : الآية الكريمة نزلت في غنائم بدر بعد الفراغ عن القتال وانهزام الكفار وأعطى سلب أبي جهل لقاتله معوذ ابن عفراء الأنصاري رضي الله عنه حين القتال فالمخصص مقارن أو مقدم لا متأخر، فليس من الباب في شيء، ولا يضرنا أن الحديث المذكور متأخر عن نزول الآية، فإنه حينئذ ليس مخصصاً بل مقرراً له هذا ما عندي وقلنا ثانياً : كما أجيب في كتب مشايخنا أنَّا لا نسلم أن الحديث المذكور مخصص إنما المخصص قوله تعالى : ﴿يَأَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ حَرْضِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ عَلَى الْقِتَالِ [الأنفال : ٦٥] وتحقيقه أن الوعد بإعطاء السلب نوع من التحريض، والأمر بالتحريض أمر مطلق، فيجوز الإتيان لكل فرد منه، وليس هذا من الاستدلال بدلالة النص بأنه لما جاز التحريض جاء إعطاء السلب أيضاً بالطريق الأولى حتى يرد أنها لا يصلح لتغيير ما ثبت بالعبارة، لكن بقي أن الجواب إنما يتم لو لم تكن هذه الآية متأخرة ولم يثبت المجيب، فالأولى أن تقرر :هكذا هذه الآية معارضة لآية الخمس البتة، فإن كانت متقدمة كما هو الظاهر أو مقارنة فليست من الباب في شيء، وإن كانت متأخرة فناسخة لكونهما مقطوعين عندنا فافهم. وقلنا ثالثاً : سلمنا التأخير لكن نمنع كونه مخصصاً ونقول : كل متراخ ناسخ لا مخصص فقيل عليه (فيه) أي في كونه ناسخاً (إبطال القاطع وهو العام الكتابي (بالمحتمل) وهو خاص خبر الواحد، وهذا لا يفيد الاستدلال. فإنه كما لا يجوز نسخ القاطع بالمحتمل كذلك لا يجوز تخصيصه به إلا أن يقال : المقصود الإلزام بأنه لا يمكنكم القول بالنسخ فأجيب بأن نسخ البعض بيان من وجه فإنه لا يبطل المنسوخ من كل وجه يبقى في البعض معمولاً (فيجوز كالتخصيص فالفرق بينه وبين النسخ (تحكم) فيجوز كلاهما، وهذا إنما يتم إن ثبا شهرة الحديث ولا بعد في دعوى الشهرة فإن الخلفاء الراشدين عملوا وتلقاه الصدر الأول بالقبول، وأما إذا كان خبر الواحد المغير المشهور فلا يجوز به نسخ الكتاب ولا تخصيصه عندنا فلا تحكم
That it is a [word] that diverts, and that contradicts the necessities of Arabic, and also we do not believe it to be a contract nor dissolution nor truth nor falsehood, for it may be a metaphor (majaz) whose qarina appears later, or a specified term (mukhassas) whose specifier appears later. This view of definitiveness is more apparent, so reflect. The Shafi'is said: Firstly, the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings upon him and his family and companions) made the spoil of the slain (salab) for the killer absolutely, whether the Imam permitted or not, as is the view of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, or only by the Imam's opinion as is the view of Abu Hanifa and Malik, after the verse: {And know that whatever you take as spoils, then indeed, for Allah is one-fifth of it and for the Messenger} [al-Anfal:41] – the verse was general necessitating the obligation of khums from the spoil, so they specified the spoil from it in a delayed manner. They said the specifier is his saying (peace and blessings upon him and his family and companions): 'Whoever kills a slain, his spoil belongs to him,' narrated by the two Shaykhs (Bukhari and Muslim). The two Imams al-Shafi'i and Ahmad interpreted it as general legislation, making the killer entitled to it, while the two Imams Abu Hanifa and Malik said: This was his permission as an Imam, so it does not establish the killer's entitlement absolutely, and this is the more correct. It is supported by his (peace be upon him) ordering Khalid ibn al-Walid (may Allah be pleased with him) and he did not give the spoil to the killer, so he complained to Allah, so he asked him, and he said: 'We considered it much, O Messenger of Allah,' so that killer said a word to Khalid, and the Messenger of Allah became angry with him, yet he did not rebuke Khalid nor deny him, and this is mentioned in Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud. We said: Firstly, the noble verse was revealed concerning the spoils of Badr after the completion of fighting and the defeat of the disbelievers, and he gave the spoil of Abu Jahl to his killer, Mu'awwidh ibn 'Afra al-Ansari (may Allah be pleased with him) at the time of fighting, so the specifier is simultaneous or preceding, not delayed, so it is not part of the issue at all. It does not harm us that the mentioned hadith is delayed after the revelation of the verse, for in that case it is not a specifier but rather a confirmator. This is what I have. And we said secondly: As answered in the books of our scholars, we do not concede that the mentioned hadith is a specifier; rather the specifier is the saying of Allah: {O Prophet, urge the believers to fight} [al-Anfal:65]. Its verification is that the promise of giving the spoil is a type of urging, and the command to urge is absolute, so each individual instance of it is permissible. This is not from inference by implication of the text (dalalat al-nass) such that when urging is permissible, giving the spoil also comes by primary inference, so that it is objected that it is not suitable for changing what is established by explicit wording. But there remains that the answer is only valid if this verse were not delayed and the respondent did not establish [the delay]. The more appropriate is to assert: This verse opposes the verse of khums absolutely; if it is preceding, as is apparent, or simultaneous, then it is not part of the issue at all; if it is delayed, then it is abrogating since both are definitive according to us, so understand. And we said thirdly: We concede the delay, but we deny that it is a specifier; we say: Every delayed [text] is an abrogator, not a specifier. So it was objected: In its being an abrogator, there is an invalidation of the definitive (the general Qur'anic text) by the probable (the specific solitary hadith), and this does not benefit the inference. For just as it is not permissible to abrogate the definitive by the probable, likewise it is not permissible to specify it by it, unless it is said: The purpose is to compel, that you cannot claim abrogation. So it was answered that abrogation of a part is clarification from one perspective, for it does not invalidate the abrogated text from every perspective; it remains operative in some parts, so it is permissible like specification, and the difference between it and abrogation is arbitrary, so both are permissible. This is only valid if the hadith is established as well-known (mashhur), and there is no difficulty in claiming notoriety, for the rightly guided caliphs acted upon it and the early generation received it with acceptance. As for a solitary hadith that is not well-known, it is not permissible to abrogate the Book by it nor to specify it according to us, so there is no arbitrariness.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage presents a debate between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools over the validity of delayed specification (takhsis) of a general Qur'anic verse by a solitary hadith (khabar wahid). The Shafi'is argue that the hadith 'Whoever kills a slain, his spoil belongs to him' specifies the general rule of khums in Surah al-Anfal, verse 41, even though the hadith was narrated after the verse. The Hanafis respond with three arguments. First, the verse was revealed after the Battle of Badr, and the hadith was already in practice, so the specification was simultaneous or even preceding, not delayed. Second, the real specifier is another verse (al-Anfal:65) urging believers to fight, which is an absolute command that includes giving the spoil as an incentive. Third, even if we assume the hadith came after the verse, delayed specification is not allowed because a definitive text cannot be specified by a probable one; rather, it would be abrogation (naskh), which is also impermissible by a solitary hadith unless it is well-known (mashhur). The passage ultimately argues that the Hanafi position is more correct, as the Shafi'i claim would entail either an impossibility or an unjustified distinction between specification and abrogation.

Key Terms
تخصيص (takhsīṣ): Specification of a general term (ʿāmm) to exclude some of its individuals.
ناسخ (nāsikh): An abrogating text that supersedes a previous text.
عام (ʿāmm): A term that encompasses all individuals of its category without restriction.
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wāḥid): A solitary hadith that does not reach the level of tawātur.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what is the status of the hadith 'من قتل قتيلاً فله سلبه' in relation to the verse of khums (al-Anfal:41)?
A) It is a delayed specifier (mukhassis muta'akhkhar) of the verse.
B) It is either simultaneous or preceding the verse, or it is a confirmator not a specifier.
C) It abrogates the verse completely.
D) It is invalid as evidence because it is not well-known.

Key Takeaway
Delayed specification of a definitive (qat'i) text by a probable (zanni) text is not allowed in the Hanafi school; it would constitute abrogation, which is also impermissible.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

Bayan al-Mujmal vs. Delayed Takhsis: The Case of Nuh's Son
Hanafi rebuttal to Shafi'i delayed takhsis argument

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between bayan al-mujmal and delayed takhsis in the Hanafi school, and apply the analysis to the story of Nuh (AS) to determine the legal category of the term 'ahl'.

Core Idea
The Hanafis treat 'ahl' as mujmal (ambiguous), not 'amm, so its clarification is bayan, not takhsis.

This passage presents a classic usul dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the interpretation of the story of Prophet Nuh (AS). The Shafi'is argue that the exclusion of Nuh's son from the term 'ahl' (family) is a case of delayed takhsis (specification) of a general term. The Hanafis respond that 'ahl' is not a general term ('amm) but an ambiguous one (mujmal), and the later verse clarifies which meaning was intended. This distinction has significant implications for the permissibility of delaying clarification beyond the time of need. Let us work through the Hanafi argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i Claim
The Shafi'is use the story of Nuh (Hud 11:40-46) as evidence that a general term can be specified later. They claim that 'ahl' initially included Nuh's son, but was later excluded by the verse 'He is not of your family'.
This is the claim of delayed takhsis.
2
State the Hanafi Response: Bayan al-Mujmal
The Hanafis reject that this is takhsis. Instead, they argue that 'ahl' is an ambiguous term (mujmal) with multiple possible meanings: relatives (haqiqah) and followers (shā'i' usage). The later verse clarifies which meaning is intended—namely, believing followers.
The clarification is called bayan al-mujmal or bayan taqrir.
3
Analyze the Linguistic Argument
The word 'ahl' is not a general term ('amm) in Hanafi usul because it does not have a single clear meaning covering all instances. Its ambiguity requires external clarification. The exception (except those against whom the word has preceded) is disconnected (munqati') because followers are not subject to that exception.
A disconnected exception supports the idea that the intended meaning was not the general category.
4
Address the Timing Objection
The Shafi'is might argue that the clarification came after the command to board, which could be a problem if it were takhsis. The Hanafis respond that since it is bayan, not takhsis, the timing does not violate any usul principles. Moreover, Nuh's assumption that his son was included was based on ijtihad or presumption of faith.
Delaying bayan beyond the time of need is permissible if the term is inherently ambiguous.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical consequence: For Hanafis, delayed takhsis of a qat'i (definitive) text by a zanni (speculative) text is invalid. But here, the issue is about the nature of the term, not timing. The Hanafis uphold that clarification of a mujmal can be delayed without issue.
The dispute shows how different conceptions of 'amm vs. mujmal affect usul reasoning.

الابن ووقت الامتثال قبله، كما قص الله تعالى من وقال : ارْكَبُوا فِيهَا بِسْمِ اللَّهِ تَجْرِيهَا وَمُرْسَهَا إِنَّ رَبِّي لَغَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ وَهِيَ تَجْرِي بِهِمْ فِي مَوج كالجِبَالِ وَنَادَى نُوحٌ ضعف استدلالهم بوجه آخر فإنه لو صح دليلهم لزم تأخير المخصص عن وقت الحاجة وهو ممتنع ،اتفاقاً، فالأصوب أن يسقط عن الجواب حديث بيان الإجمال، ويقال إنه بيان تقرير فإن المراد بالأهل الاتباع وكان محفوفاً ،بالقرينة، وأمره عليه السلام ابنه بالركوب إما لزعم الإيمان لكونه كافراً منافقاً، أو حمل الأهل على ذي النسب بالاجتهاد فقرر
The third article on linguistic principles. (And) they said secondly: Allah said to Nuh (upon our Prophet and his family and him peace): {Until when Our command came and the oven overflowed, We said, 'Carry in it of every [kind] two mates, and your family – except those against whom the word has preceded – and whoever has believed. And none believed with him except a few'} [Hud:40]. And 'family' (ahl) included the son, and the exclusion of his son was delayed by His saying: {Indeed, he is not of your family; indeed, he is [one whose] work is other than righteous} [Hud:46] ... (We said: We do not concede that it is a specifier; rather it is a clarification of the ambiguous term (mujmal), namely the word 'ahl', for it is common for lineage and is a literal (haqiqah) in it, and it is common for followers (atba') and used in both like the use of the literal. So Allah clarified by His saying {Indeed, he is not of your family} that 'ahl' means the believing followers. On this basis, the exception {except those against whom the word has preceded} is disconnected (munqati'), for among the followers there is none against whom the word has preceded. Then, on the assumption that followers are intended, it should not mean absolute followers, but those who also have a relation of kinship with him, otherwise the conjunctive {and whoever has believed} would be lost... (Then a discussion about timing and the permissibility of delaying clarification.) ... And whoever contemplates this story knows that the time of compliance with the command to embark was at the moment of the oven's eruption and the coming of the great sign before the arrival of drowning. From here the weakness of their argument is evident from another angle: for if their proof were valid, it would necessitate delaying the specifier beyond the time of need, which is unanimously prohibited. Therefore, the more correct is to drop the answer about clarification of the ambiguous (tabyin al-mujmal) and say it is a clarification of confirmation (bayan taqrir), for the intended meaning of 'ahl' is followers, and it was accompanied by a qarina (contextual clue). He (peace be upon him) commanded his son to embark either due to assuming his faith – for he was a hypocrite, his condition concealed from him until revelation came, as said by Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi – or due to his ijtihad in interpreting 'ahl' as relatives, and error in ijtihad is permissible for prophets according to Ahl al-Haqq, provided they do not persist. So he settled on that.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents the second Shafi'i argument for delayed takhsis, using the story of Prophet Nuh (Noah). The Shafi'is argue that the general term 'ahl' (family) in the verse initially included Nuh's son, but was later specified by the verse excluding him. The Hanafis respond that this is not takhsis but rather bayan al-mujmal (clarification of an ambiguous term). The word 'ahl' is ambiguous: it can mean relatives (haqiqah) or followers (also common usage). Allah's later statement clarifies that the intended meaning is 'believing followers', not relatives. Thus, the son was never included. The Hanafis also discuss the timing issue: the clarification occurred after the command to board, but they argue that because 'ahl' was already ambiguous and accompanied by contextual clues, the clarification is valid as a bayan taqrir (confirmatory clarification). They further argue that even if it were considered takhsis, it would be delayed beyond the time of need, which is impossible. The passage concludes that the correct view is the Hanafi one, dismissing the Shafi'i claim.

Key Terms
مجمل (mujmal): A word that has multiple possible meanings and requires clarification (bayan).
بيان (bayan): Clarification of a mujmal term, revealing the intended meaning.
منقطع (munqati'): A disconnected exception, where the exception is not part of the general category.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification of a general term to exclude some of its instances.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis in this lesson, why is the exclusion of Nuh's son from 'ahl' considered bayan al-mujmal rather than delayed takhsis?
A) Because the word 'ahl' is a general term ('amm) and the later verse specifies it.
B) Because the word 'ahl' is ambiguous (mujmal) between relatives and followers, and the later verse clarifies the intended meaning.
C) Because the exception 'except those against whom the word has preceded' is connected.
D) Because the command to embark was unconditional.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes sharply between 'amm (general) and mujmal (ambiguous); the story of Nuh illustrates that what appears to be delayed specification is actually clarification of an ambiguous term.

The Story of Noah and the Term 'Ahl' – Delayed Bayan vs. Delayed Takhsis
Defending delayed bayan via the Noah narrative

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between bayan al-mujmal and takhsis to the Noah narrative and evaluate the opposing argument.

Core Idea
The Noah narrative proves delayed bayan of a mujmal, not delayed takhsis of an amm.

This passage from the third article on linguistic principles defends the Hanafi position that delayed specification (takhsis) is impermissible, but delayed clarification (bayan) of an ambiguous term is allowed. The opponent cites Noah's story to argue for delayed takhsis, but the Hanafi author reinterprets it as bayan al-mujmal using the homonymy of 'ahl'.

Guided Path
1
State the opponent's argument
The opponent claims that the Quran initially commanded Noah to take his family (ahl), which apparently included his son, and later specified that the son is not of his family, proving delayed takhsis.
The opponent relies on the apparent meaning of 'ahl' as including all relatives.
2
Identify the Hanafi objection
The Hanafi author objects that 'ahl' is not a general term (amm) but a homonym (mushtarak) used for relatives and followers. Thus the later verse clarifies which meaning is intended, not that the original was general and then specified.
This makes the passage an example of bayan al-mujmal, not takhsis.
3
Analyze the timing objection
The opponent argues that the clarification came after the time of need (the command to embark), which is impermissible for bayan. The Hanafi response is that bayan of a mujmal can be delayed because the command was conditional on subsequent clarification; the ambiguity was resolved later.
This is a key difference: delayed takhsis is prohibited, but delayed bayan is allowed.
4
Explore alternative interpretations
The author also presents other readings: Noah assumed his son was a believer (hypocrite), or he made an ijtihad error, or the exception always excluded the son because the word of punishment had already gone forth against disbelievers.
These alternative interpretations further support that the original verse did not definitively include the son.
5
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: if delayed takhsis were allowed, general commands would not be binding until specification, causing uncertainty. Hanafis restrict this to bayan al-mujmal, preserving the binding nature of amm.
This shows the difference in legal methodology.

بعد غرق الابن ووقت الامتثال قبله، كما قص الله تعالى من وقال : ارْكَبُوا فِيهَا بِسْمِ اللَّهِ تَجْرِيهَا وَمُرْسَهَا إِنَّ رَبِّي لَغَفُورٌ رَّحِيمٌ وَهِيَ تَجْرِي بِهِمْ فِي مَوج كالجِبَالِ وَنَادَى نُوحٌ ابْنَهُ وَكَانَ فِي مَعْزِلٍ يَبُنَى ارْكَب مَعَنَا وَلَا تَكُن مَّعَ الْكَفِرِينَ قَالَ سَنَاوِي إِلَى جبَل يَعْصِمُنِي مِنَ الْمَاءِ قَالَ لَا عَاصِمَ الْيَوْمَ مِنْ أَمْرِ اللَّهِ إِلَّا مَن رَّحِم وَحَالَ بَيْنَهُمَا الْمَوْجُ فَكَانَ مِنَ الْمُغْرَقِينَ وَقِيلَ يَتَأَرْضُ ابْلَعِي مَاءَكِ وَيَسَمَاءُ أَقْلِعِي وَغِيضَ الْمَاءُ وَقُضِيَ الْأَمْرُ وَاسْتَوَتْ عَلَى الْجُودِي وَقِيلَ بُعْدًا لِلْقَوْمِ الظَّلِمِينَ ) وَنَادَى نُوحٌ رَّبَّهُ ﴾ [هود : ٤١ - ٤٥] الآية. ومن تأمل في هذه القصة علم أن وقت الامتثال بالأمر بالإركاب هو وقت فور التنور ومجيء الآية الكبرى قبل وصول الغرق، ومن ههنا تبين ضعف استدلالهم بوجه آخر فإنه لو صح دليلهم لزم تأخير المخصص عن وقت الحاجة وهو ممتنع ،اتفاقاً، فالأصوب أن يسقط عن الجواب حديث بيان الإجمال، ويقال إنه بيان تقرير فإن المراد بالأهل الاتباع وكان محفوفاً ،بالقرينة، وأمره عليه السلام ابنه بالركوب إما لزعم الإيمان لكونه كافراً منافقاً، أو حمل الأهل على ذي النسب بالاجتهاد فقرر الله تعالى ما أراده فلهذا عاتبه على الخطأ وهو تعوذ أو المراد بالأهل القريب سبباً ونسباً بقرينة ما كانت والابن داخل في المستثنى وهو كان عالماً بأن المراد ممن سبق الكفار لكن كان يظنه عليه السلام مؤمنا لنفاقه داخلاً في الباقي بعد الاستثناء ومن سبق عليه القول مختصاً بامرأته، ولا ذنب في هذا الخطأ في الاجتهاد كما زعم بعض الملاحدة من الروافض وغيرهم فإنه مخالفة حكمه قصداً وهذا امتثال به قصداً فهو محل الثواب ووجه العتاب عليه أن حسنات الأبرار سيئات المقربين فافهم وتثبت ويمكن أن يقال : إن نداء نوح ابنه كان كناية عن طلب الإيمان أي آمن فاركب معنا رجاء أن يهتدي عند رؤية الآية الكبرى، فلما لم يهتد نادى ربه بأنه من أهلي فطمعت في إيمانه ولأنه أهل موعود بالنجاة ووعدك الحق من إغراق الكفرة ونجاة المؤمنين يحكم بأنه مات كافراً فأنا متحير فيه فعاتبه تعالى على تعبيره بالأهل إذ شأن الرسل أرفع من أن يقولوا للكفرة أهلهم بل لهم أن يتبرؤوا منهم ويعبروهم بالأعداء، هذا تأويل حسن لا يحتاج إلى القول بالخطأ في الاجتهاد، لكن يأبى عنه قوله تعالى: ﴿وَأُوحِيَ إِلَى نُوح أَنَّهُ لَن يُؤْمِنَ مِن قَوْمِكَ إِلَّا مَن قَدْ ءَامَنَ ﴾ [هود: ٣٦] إلا أن يقال : المتبادر من القوم البعداء لا القريب المحض كالابن فهو مسكوت عنه هذا والله أعلم بمعاني كتابه والأسرار التي وقعت بينه وبين خواص عباده
The third article on linguistic principles. Its specification with us, so do not rule. And they said, secondly: Allah Almighty said to Noah (upon him and our Prophet and his family peace): Until when Our command came and the oven overflowed, We said: Carry in it from every pair two, and your family except those against whom the word has already gone forth, and those who believe. And none believed with him except a few (Hud 11:40). And 'family' included the son, and the exclusion of his son was delayed by His saying: Indeed, he is not of your family; indeed, he is an unrighteous deed (Hud 11:46). He called out that he was from him as Allah textually stated: And Noah called out to his Lord and said: My Lord, indeed my son is of my family, and indeed Your promise is true, and You are the most just of judges. He said: O Noah, indeed he is not of your family; indeed, he is an unrighteous deed, so do not ask Me that of which you have no knowledge (Hud 11:45-46). (We say: we do not concede that it is a specification; rather it is an explanation of the ambiguous (mujmal), namely) the word 'family', for it is prevalent in lineage and is a reality therein, and (it is) prevalent in (followers) and used in both like the use of reality. So Allah explained by His saying: Indeed, he is not of your family (Hud 11:46) that 'family' means the believing followers. On this basis, the exception by His saying: except those against whom the word has already gone forth (Hud 11:40) is disjoined, for among the followers there is none against whom the word has gone forth. Then, assuming the intention of followers, absolute followers should not be intended, but rather those who also have a relationship of kinship, otherwise the conjunction of 'and those who believe' (Hud 11:40) would be lost. (Or) the exception is ambiguous, namely 'except those against whom the word has already gone forth'. On this, the intended meaning of 'family' is the family by lineage so that the ambiguous exception is connected and effective in making the general ambiguous. If you say: If the intended meaning of 'family' was followers, what is the meaning of Noah's saying: indeed my son is of my family? He said: Noah's saying 'my son is of my family' was due to his assumption of his faith, for he was a hypocrite, his state hidden from him until revelation descended, according to what was said - the speaker is Imam al-Huda Sheikh Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (may Allah have mercy on him). This is not impossible regarding prophets. (Or he assumed the intention of lineage) and said: indeed my son is of my family, and error in ijtihad is permissible for them according to the people of truth, provided they do not persist. Then there is a discussion here: this cannot be a bayan of the mujmal, for delay is not permissible in it from the time of need, and here it has been delayed from the time of compliance with the command to embark. And what was said: the command is absolute in time, so the time of compliance is the duration of life, so there is no delay - is rejected, for the time of compliance is the command of Allah the great sign. Moreover, this was after the drowning of the son and the time of compliance was before it, as Allah narrated: And he said: Embark in it; in the name of Allah is its sailing and its anchorage. Indeed, my Lord is Forgiving and Merciful. And it sailed with them through waves like mountains, and Noah called out to his son who was in isolation: O my son, embark with us and be not with the disbelievers. He said: I will take refuge on a mountain that will protect me from the water. He said: There is no protector today from the command of Allah except for whom He has mercy. And the waves came between them, and he was among the drowned. And it was said: O earth, swallow your water, and O sky, cease, and the water subsided, and the command was fulfilled, and it settled on Judi, and it was said: Away with the wrongdoing people. And Noah called out to his Lord (Hud 11:41-45). And whoever contemplates this story knows that the time of compliance with the command to embark is at the moment of the oven's overflow and the coming of the great sign before the arrival of drowning. From here, the weakness of their argument is shown in another respect: if their proof were valid, it would necessitate delaying the specification from the time of need, which is impossible by consensus. So the more correct approach is to drop the answer based on bayan al-ijmal, and to say it is bayan taqrir (explanatory confirmation), for the intended meaning of 'family' was followers, and it was accompanied by a qarina. And his (peace be upon him) ordering his son to embark was either due to assuming faith because he was a disbelieving hypocrite, or he interpreted 'family' as lineage by ijtihad. So Allah confirmed what He intended, therefore He rebuked him for the error - and this is a refuge. Or the intended meaning of 'family' is close relative by cause and lineage, due to the qarina that existed, and the son is included in the excepted. And he (Noah) knew that the intended meaning of 'those who preceded' was the disbelievers, but he assumed him to be a believer due to his hypocrisy, so he was included in the remainder after the exception. And 'those against whom the word has gone forth' was specific to his wife. There is no sin in this error of ijtihad, as some heretics among the Rafidah and others claim; for it is knowingly contradicting His ruling, and this is intentionally complying with it, so it is a place of reward. And the aspect of rebuke is that the good deeds of the pious are the bad deeds of the near ones. So understand and be firm. And it can be said: Noah's calling to his son was a metonymy for seeking faith, i.e., believe and embark with us, hoping he would be guided upon seeing the great sign. When he was not guided, he called upon his Lord saying he is of my family, so I desired his faith, and because he was a family promised salvation, and Your promise is true - the drowning of disbelievers and salvation of believers - (so) it rules that he died a disbeliever, so I am perplexed about him. So Allah rebuked him for his expression 'family', for the manner of messengers is higher than to call disbelievers their family; rather they should disown them and call them enemies. This is a good interpretation that does not require claiming error in ijtihad. However, it is precluded by Allah's saying: And it was revealed to Noah that none of your people will believe except those who have already believed (Hud 11:36), unless it be said: the dominant usage of 'people' is distant ones, not the immediate relative like a son, so it is left unaddressed. This, and Allah knows best the meanings of His Book and the secrets between Him and His special servants.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage opens the third article on linguistic principles. It is a disputation (usul dispute) where the Hanafi author responds to an opponent's argument that the Quran permits delayed specification (takhsis). The opponent cites the story of Noah: initially, the term 'ahl' (family) in the command to Noah included his son, but later it was specified to exclude him. The Hanafi response is that this is not specification but rather bayan al-mujmal (clarification of an ambiguous term). The word 'ahl' is a mushtarak (homonym) used for both relatives and followers; Allah's later statement 'he is not of your family' clarifies that here it means believing followers, not that the original was general. The author then addresses the objection that this bayan came after the time of need (the command to embark). He refutes it by arguing that the command was immediate and the bayan came after the drowning, but this is not a problem because the bayan is of a mujmal, and mujmal can be clarified later. Alternatively, the story can be interpreted as Noah's own ijtihad error in thinking his son was a believer. The author also presents a third view: the term 'ahl' includes relatives, but the exception 'except those against whom the word has gone forth' specifically excludes the son because the word of punishment had gone forth against disbelieving relatives. The passage ends with a discussion of the permissibility of prophetic ijtihad and the theological point about the high status of prophets.

Key Terms
أهل (ahl): The term 'ahl' is mushtarak (homonym) used both for relatives and followers, and in this context it is ambiguous (mujmal).
مجمل (mujmal): An expression that is ambiguous due to homonymy or lack of clarity, requiring external clarification (bayan).
بيان (bayan): Clarification of an ambiguous term (mujmal) or specification of a general term under certain conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, the verse 'he is not of your family' is an example of:
A) Takhsis (specification) of a general term
B) Bayan (clarification) of a mujmal (ambiguous) term
C) Naskh (abrogation) of a previous ruling
D) Taqyid (restriction) of an absolute term

Key Takeaway
The Noah narrative is a case of delayed bayan (clarification of an ambiguous term), not delayed takhsis (specification of a general term) – a key Hanafi usul distinction.

Amm and Khass — General and Specific

The Hanafi Refutation of Delayed Specification from al-Anbiya 21:98-101
Refuting delayed specification via contextual restriction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of contextual restriction to Quranic verses and evaluate the claim of delayed specification.

Core Idea
A general Quranic verse is understood in light of its audience and context; delayed specification is rejected when the 'generality' is actually restricted from the start.

This lesson examines a key usul dispute: whether the verse 'you and what you worship are fuel of Hell' was later specified by 'those for whom the best has preceded'. Opponents argue it is an example of delayed takhsis. The Hanafis respond by showing the verse was never general in the first place due to contextual restriction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opposing Claim
The opponents (often associated with the Mutakallimun) argue that verse 21:98 was general, including all worshipped beings, and that verse 21:101 was revealed later as a specification excluding Christ, Ezra, and angels.
This is a classic challenge against the Hanafi position that takhsis al-nass cannot be delayed.
2
Critique the Opponents' Proof: The Hadith on 'ma'
The opponents cite a hadith where the Prophet allegedly said 'ma' is for non-intelligent beings. The Hanafis establish that this hadith is baseless (la asla lahu) and thus cannot be used to restrict the meaning of 'ma' to non-intelligent beings only.
Even if the hadith were sound, Hanafis argue it would only apply to one usage, not the general rule.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Linguistic Argument
The Hanafis argue that the relative clause 'ma ta'buduna' (what you worship) is restricted by the addressees. The verse is addressing the Meccan idolaters, so 'what you worship' refers specifically to their idols (al-asnam). Thus, Christ, Ezra, and angels were never included.
This aligns with the usul principle that a mawsul's generality is limited by its sila (the clause that describes it).
4
Understand the Contextual Restriction Principle
The Hanafi school holds that when a verse addresses a specific audience and refers to their specific practices, the ruling applies only to that context unless there is a clear indication of generality. Here, the mention of 'you' (line 21:98) points to the Meccans.
This principle prevents unnecessary claims of delayed specification and preserves the immediate binding force of texts.
5
Derive the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
If delayed specification were accepted, any general text could be reinterpreted later, weakening legal certainty. Hanafis restrict such claims to preserve the integrity of revealed rulings from the moment of revelation.
The dispute is not just about one verse; it reflects a fundamental difference in usul methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) قالوا (ثالثاً) قوله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ لَهُم مِّنَا الْحُسْنَى أُولَبِكَ عَنْهَا [الأنبياء: ۱۰۱] (نزل) مخصصاً بعد اعتراض ابن الزبعرى على قوله: ﴿إِنَّكُمْ وَمَا تَعْبُدُونَ مِن دُونِ اللَّهِ حَصَبُ جَهَنَّمَ [الأنبياء: ۹۸] بأن المسيح عبده النصارى، وعزيراً عبده اليهود، والملائكة عبدهم بنو المليح، فخصص إياهم متراخياً، فإن قلت روي أنه عليه وآله الصلاة والسلام قال في دفع اعتراضه : ما أجهلك بلغة قومك إن ما لما لا يعقل أجاب بقوله (وما عرف أنه صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم قال : ما أجهلك بلغة قومك ما لما لا يعقل فلا أصل له كما بينا قبل وقرر هذا الجواب في كلام كبار مشايخنا بأن المسيح والعزير والملائكة غير داخلين فإن ما لما لا يعقل ولم يتمسك بالحديث، وهذا إنما يصح على رأي من يخصص ما بغير العقلاء، وأما على ما هو المشهور من العقلاء وغيرهم فلا (قلنا) لا نسلم عمومه مطلقاً للمعبودين كلهم بل (عمومه إنما هو في معبود المخاطبين وهم أهل مكة (وهو الأصنام كما ذكره السهيلي فإن الموصول إنما يعم في الموصوفين بالصلة (فلم يتناول عيسى والملائكة) وعزيراً فاعتراضه تعنت والنزول بقوله تعالى : وإِنَّ الَّذِينَ سَبَقَتْ ﴾ [هود : ١٠١] الآية (تصريح بما علم من عدم دخولهم (أو) تأسيس لبيان بعدهم عنها فضلاً عن الدخول فيها قطعاً لتعنت الأشقياء (وليس) النزول بتخصيص فتدبر)
(And) they said (thirdly): His statement, the Exalted: Indeed, those for whom the best [reward] has preceded from Us are those who are far from it [the Fire] (al-Anbiya 21:101) was revealed as a specification after the objection of Ibn al-Ziba'ra to His statement: Indeed, you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell (al-Anbiya 21:98) because the Christians worship Christ, the Jews worship Ezra, and the angels are worshipped by the polytheists. So He specified them (i.e., excluded them) belatedly. If you say: it is narrated that he (peace and blessings be upon him) said in repelling his objection: 'How ignorant you are of your people's language; 'ma' is for non-intelligent beings.' He replied: (and it is not known that he صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم said: 'How ignorant you are of your people's language; 'ma' is for non-intelligent beings' - it has no basis as we clarified before. And this answer is established in the statements of our senior scholars: that Christ, Ezra, and the angels are not included, because 'ma' is for non-intelligent beings, and they did not adhere to the hadith. This is only valid according to the opinion of one who restricts 'ma' to non-intelligent beings, but according to what is well-known that it includes intelligent and non-intelligent beings, it is not. (We say) we do not concede its generality absolutely for all worshipped beings; rather, its generality is only concerning the worshipped beings of the addressees, i.e., the people of Mecca, and they are the idols, as mentioned by al-Suhayli. For the relative pronoun (alladhi) only generalizes over those described by the relative clause. So it did not include Jesus, the angels, and Ezra. So his objection is stubbornness, and the revelation of the verse 'Indeed, those for whom the best [reward] has preceded' (Hud 11:101) is a declaration of what is known of their non-inclusion, or a foundation for stating their distance from it, let alone their inclusion in it, to cut off the stubbornness of the wretched. And the revelation is not a specification, so reflect.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on delayed specification with a third argument from the opponents. They claim that the verse 'Indeed, you and what you worship besides Allah are fuel of Hell' (al-Anbiya 21:98) was general, including Christ, Ezra, and angels, but then the later verse 'Indeed, those for whom the best [reward] has preceded from Us are those who are far from it' (21:101) specified them out belatedly. The Hanafi response has two parts: First, the narrated hadith that 'ma' is for non-intelligent beings is unreliable. Second, even without that, the generality of the first verse is not absolute; it addresses the idolaters of Mecca and refers specifically to their idols (al-asnam). The relative clause 'ma ta'buduna' (what you worship) is restricted by the context of the address. Since Christ, Ezra, and angels are not among the idols of the Meccans, they were never included in the threat. Thus the later verse does not specify; it merely confirms what was already known. The author concludes that the revelation of the second verse was not a specification but a confirmation or a stronger statement of their exclusion.

Key Terms
ما (ma): A relative pronoun or particle that can be used for non-intelligent beings, but in this context it is part of 'ma ta'buduna' meaning 'what you worship'.
موصول (mawsul): Relative pronoun; the generality of the mawsul is limited by the description (sila) that follows.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response, why were Christ, Ezra, and angels not included in the verse 'you and what you worship are fuel of Hell'?
A) Because the word 'ma' only refers to non-intelligent beings
B) Because the verse was abrogated before it could apply to them
C) Because the verse specifically addresses the Meccan idolaters and their idols
D) Because they were mentioned in a different verse

Key Takeaway
Contextual restriction is a key Hanafi tool that prevents claims of delayed specification and preserves the immediate legal force of general texts.

The Khums Verse: Did It Undergo Delayed Takhsis?
Addressing the claim that the khums verse was later specified to exclude certain clans, and critiquing a weak defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the argument that the khums verse was subject to delayed takhsis and identify the Hanafi commentator's critique of the matn's defense.

Core Idea
The khums verse's general term 'dhi al-qurba' cannot be defended as always restricted to close relatives because the inclusion of Banu al-Muttalib and exclusion of equally related clans proves delayed specification occurred.

In this lesson, we examine a key usul al-fiqh dispute: whether a general Quranic verse can be considered to have been later specified (takhsis) by the Prophet's practice. The opponent argues that the khums verse was initially general for all relatives, then the Prophet excluded Banu Abd Shams and Banu Nawfal. The matn author (of Musallam al-Thubut) defends that the term 'qurba' always meant close relatives, so no delayed takhsis occurred. But the commentator exposes a fatal flaw in that defense, forcing us to reconsider how we apply the rules of general and specific in Quranic interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Opponent's Claim
Recognize that the opponent asserts the khums verse was general (amm) and later specified (takhsis) when the Prophet excluded two clans from the share of khums for relatives.
The verse: 'fa-anna lillahi khumusahu wa lil-rasuli wa li-dhi al-qurba' (al-Anfal 8:41). The term 'dhi al-qurba' is ostensibly general for all relatives.
2
State the Matn Author's Defense
The author of Musallam al-Thubot responds that 'qurba' here means close relatives only, so Banu Abd Shams and Banu Nawfal were never included in the general term. Thus no delayed takhsis occurred.
This defense relies on the claim that the word 'qurba' itself is ambiguous and can be restricted contextually.
3
Examine the Commentator's Critique
The commentator points out that Banu al-Muttalib, Banu Abd Shams, and Banu Nawfal are all at the same degree of kinship to the Prophet. Yet only Banu al-Muttalib were included. This disproves the idea that 'qurba' inherently meant only close relatives.
If the term was always confined to close relatives, all three clans would have been excluded (or included). The differential treatment proves specification occurred.
4
Identify the Implication for Usul
The commentator's critique shows that a weak defense of agnosticism (claiming the term was never general) fails when faced with consistent historical practice. A stronger Hanafi argument would rely on a qarina (indication) from the Prophet's practice, not a semantic restriction.
This highlights the importance of historical evidence in resolving disputes over the scope of Quranic terms.
5
Conclude the Lesson's Legal Point
The passage demonstrates that a superficial defense of 'non-specification' is untenable when the evidence clearly shows differential treatment among equally related groups. The Hanafi school must either accept delayed takhsis or provide a better explanation.
Thus, the passage teaches us to scrutinize arguments for internal consistency and to avoid arbitrary semantic restrictions.

Source Text

وقالوا رابعاً: إن قوله تعالى: ﴿فَأَنَّ لِلَّهِ مُسَهُ وَلِلرَّسُولِ وَلِذِي الْقُرْبَى ﴾ [الأنفال : ٤١] كان عاماً متناولاً لكل ذي قرابة فخصص وأخرج بنو عبد شمس وبنو نوفل بعد زمان وأجاب عنه المصنف بأن القرابة وإن كانت عامة لكن المراد ههنا القرابة القريبة فهم غير داخلين في العموم، وهذا ليس بشيء، فإن بني نوفل وبني عبد شمس وبني المطلب كلهم في درجة واحدة من القرابة، وبنو المطلب داخلون فيه وأخرج بنو عبد شمس وبنو نوفل، ولهذا قال جبير بن مطعم وأمير المؤمنين
And they said fourthly: Indeed, His statement, the Exalted: So that one-fifth is for Allah and the Messenger and for the near of kin (al-Anfal 8:41) was general, including every relative, then it was specified and Banu Abd Shams and Banu Nawfal were excluded after some time. The author (of Musallam al-Thubut) answered that although 'qiraba' is general, the intended meaning here is close relatives, so they are not included in the generality. But this is nothing, for Banu Nawfal, Banu Abd Shams, and Banu al-Muttalib are all at the same degree of kinship, and Banu al-Muttalib are included while Banu Abd Shams and Banu Nawfal are excluded. That is why Jubayr ibn Mut'im and the Commander of the Faithful (said...)
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This is the fourth argument from the opponents, citing the verse on khums (spoils) from Surah al-Anfal. The phrase 'dhi al-qurba' (near of kin) is ostensibly general for all relatives, but later the Prophet (peace be upon him) excluded Banu Abd Shams and Banu Nawfal from the share. This appears to be a delayed specification. The author of Musallam al-Thubut (the matn) answered that 'qurba' here means close relatives, not all relatives, so those distant clans were never included. The commentator (in our text) critiques this answer, arguing that all three clans (Banu Abd Shams, Banu Nawfal, Banu al-Muttalib) are at the same degree of kinship to the Prophet, yet Banu al-Muttalib were included while the other two were excluded. Thus the author's answer is insufficient. The text then mentions Jubayr ibn Mut'im and the Commander of the Faithful (likely 'Umar or 'Ali) as having said something about this issue, but the passage cuts off. The commentator implies that a better response is needed, perhaps that the specification was based on additional evidence (like their support during the boycott) rather than a delayed takhsis. This passage shows an internal critique of the matn's defense, illustrating the importance of precise analysis in usul.

Key Terms
ذو القربى (dhu al-qurba): Near of kin; in this context, it is a term for relatives eligible for khums.
قرابة (qiraba): Kinship; the term can be general or specific.
تخصيص (takhsis): Specification; restricting a general term to some of its instances.
قرينة (qarina): An indication or contextual clue that clarifies the intended meaning of a text.

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator criticize the author's answer regarding the khums verse?
A) Because the author used a weak hadith
B) Because Banu al-Muttalib, Banu Abd Shams, and Banu Nawfal are all at the same degree of kinship, yet only Banu al-Muttalib were included
C) Because the verse was abrogated
D) Because the author misunderstood the meaning of 'qurba'

Key Takeaway
A claim that a general term in the Qur'an was never general must be tested against the Prophet's practice—if equally related groups are treated differently, the claim of inherent restriction fails, and one must acknowledge specification or provide a stronger evidence-based argument.

Extent of Specification: Can a General Term Be Specified to One Individual?
Dispute on the minimum number for specification of a general term

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the minimum number for takhsis and evaluate the opposing arguments using the Quranic proof from Al Imran 173.

Core Idea
Hanafis allow specification of a general term to a single individual, based on Quranic usage.

This passage examines a fundamental dispute in usul al-fiqh: to how few individuals can a general term ('amm) be narrowed by a specifier? The Hanafi madhhab takes a bold position permitting specification to one individual, relying on both rational analogy and a powerful Quranic example from Surah Al Imran. The discussion also tackles objections regarding linguistic eloquence and the nature of connected specifiers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Positions and the Core Question
State the question: 'To how many individuals can a general term be specified?' List the four views: to most, to three, to two, to one.
The Hanafi choice is to one.
2
Examine the Hanafi Proof from Analogy
Understand the argument that all specifiers (independent and connected) should be equal in effect, allowing reduction to one. Note the author's caveat about the premise.
The author questions whether the ruling is the same for independent and non-independent specifiers.
3
Analyze the Quranic Proof from Al Imran 173
Recognize how the word 'الناس' is interpreted as one person (Nu'aym ibn Mas'ud). Evaluate the counterargument that this is 'ahd (definiteness) not generality, and the Hanafi rebuttal.
Hanafis argue that 'ahd itself is a form of specification, and the condition of prior mention is not met.
4
Address the Objection from Eloquence
Consider the claim that using a general term for few individuals is linguistically ineloquent. Understand the Hanafi distinction between linguistic correctness and rhetorical elegance, and the role of a narrative purpose.
If there is a rhetorical point, the speech is not ineloquent.
5
Conclude with the Thamarah al-Khilaf
Identify the practical consequence of this dispute for interpreting legal texts: e.g., a general command like 'give to the poor' can be fulfilled by one poor person according to Hanafis, but may require three or more according to others.

التخصيص إلى كم أفراداً أي منتهى التخصيص ما هو (فالأكثر) قالوا: يجوز (إلى الأكثر) وفسر الأكثر بالزائد على النصف وهذا غير محصل، فإن أفراد العام غير محصورة في الأكثر، فلا يعلم كسوره فلا يعلم الأكثر (وقيل ينتهي إلى ثلاثة وقيل) ينتهي (إلى اثنين وقيل) ينتهي إلى واحد وهو مختار (الحنفية وما قال الإمام فخر الإسلام أن العام إن كان جمعاً فيصح تخصيصه إلى ثلاثة لأنها أقل الجمع، فالمراد منه على ما قال الشيخ ابن الهمام الجمع المنكر على ما سيجيء تحقيقه إن شاء الله تعالى لنا أوّلاً: جواز إكرم الناس إلا الجهال وإن كان العالم واحداً اتفاقاً) وسيجيء أن هذا مختلف فيه وكذا سائر المخصصات المقارنة) لأن الكل سواسية في إفادة القصر فكذا في قدره ثم هذا الاستدلال إنما يتم لو كان حكم المستقل وغير المستقل واحداً، وهو في حيز الخفاء، بل اقتران غير المستقل ليس تخصيصاً وقصراً عندنا كما مر، فلا يقاس عليه ما هو قصر، وإن خصص بغير المستقل فلا ينفع كثيراً سيما عندنا فتجويز ابن الحاجب الانتهاء (في الصفة والشرط إلى اثنين فقط) حيث قال : إنه بالاستثناء والبدل يجوز إلى الواحد وبالمتصل كالصفة يجوز إلى اثنين وبالمنفصل في المحصور القليل يجوز إلى الاثنين وفي غير المحصور إلى جمع يقرب من مدلوله (تحكم) فإن التقييدات الغير المستقلة كلها سواء، وأيضاً يجوز انحصار الموصوف بصفة في فرد واحد كما يدل عليه الاستقراء الغير المكذوب والإنكار مكابرة فافهم (و) لنا (ثانياً) قوله تعالى : الَّذِينَ قَالَ لَهُمُ النَّاسُ إِنَّ النَّاسَ قَدْ جَمَعُوا لَكُمْ ﴾ [آل عمران ۱۷۳] أي لقتالكم (والمراد) بالناس : الأول (نعيم بن مسعود باتفاق المفسرين فأريد بالعام الواحد فهو منتهى التخصيص (والجواب) كما في شرح المختصر وغيره بأن الناس للمعهود فلا عموم له فلا تخصيص فلا يثبت المدعى (مدفوع) بأن التخصيص كالعهد فإنا اشترطنا المقارنة في المخصص) فالعام المخصوص أريد به بعض ما يتناوله بدلالة أمر مقارن، كذلك في المعهود أريد بعض ما يتناوله الصيغة بدلالة اللام المقارن، وردّ بأنه لا شك أن المعهود غير عام حقيقة، فلا يمكن أن يدعي أن إرادة البعض في المعهود نوع من تخصيص العام فلم يبق إلا قياس التخصيص على إرادة البعض في المعهود، وهو قياس في اللغة فلا هذا، واعلم أن دفع هذا السؤال سهل فإن من

انحط الكلام عن درجة البلاغة قال : (وأما انحطاط الكلام عن درجة البلاغة فليس الكلام فيه وإنما الكلام في الصحة لغة ثم الانحطاط إنما يكون إذا لم يكن التعبير بالعام عن الثلاثة أو الواحد لنكتة، وحينئذ ينحط الكلام أيضاً إذا بقي أكثر عند خلو التعبير عن النكتة، وأما إذا كان نكتة كما إذا كان الثلاثة أو الواحد بحيث يكون قوام البلد بهم وقد قتلهم وقال : قلت : كل من البلد إقامة لهم مقام الكل فالانحطاط ممنوع ، وبما ذكرنا اندفع ما يقال : إن المقصود من المسألة أن يحمل في الكلام الإلهي والحديث النبوي على التخصيص إلى الواحد أو الاثنين، ولما كان هذا موجباً لانحطاط الكلام عن درجة البلاغة لا يمكن حمل الكلامين، وهما أفصحا كل كلام عداهما من كلام البشر عليه، وإذا سلم المجيب الانحطاط فقد لزم أن لا التخصيص إلى الثلاثة وما دونه في كلام الشارع فتدبر المجوزون إلى الثلاثة أو الاثنين (قالوا : إنه قصر للعام على بعض المسمى (وهو) أي المسمى (في الجمع ثلاثة) عند المجيز إلى الثلاثة (أو اثنان) عند المجيز إلى الاثنين : فإن قلت : هذا الاستدلال لا يعم المطلوب، فإن العام ربما كان غير الجمع، قال: (ولعلهم جوزوا التخصيص (في غير الجمع إلى الواحد) وهذا على الإطلاق غير صحيح، فإن الشيخ أبا بكر بن القفال قد سوّى بين صيغ العموم جمعاً كان أو
Issue: To how many individuals does specification (takhsis) extend? That is, what is the limit of specification? (The majority) said: It is permissible to the most (al-akthar), and they interpreted 'most' as more than half. But this is not precise, since the individuals of the general term are not limited to 'most,' so its fraction is unknown, hence 'most' is unknown. (And it was said it ends at three, and it was said it ends at two, and it was said it ends at one, which is the choice of the Hanafis. And what Imam Fakhr al-Islam said that if the general term is a plural, its specification is valid to three because three is the least of the plural; but according to what Ibn al-Humann said, it is the indefinite plural as will be verified. For us, first: it is permissible to honor people except the ignorant, even if the knowledgeable one is a single person by agreement). And it will come that this is disputed, and likewise all the connected specifiers. Because all are equal in effecting restriction, so likewise in its extent. Then this reasoning is only valid if the ruling of the independent and non-independent specifier are the same, which is obscure. Rather, according to us, the connection of a non-independent specifier is not specification and restriction, as passed, so it cannot be analogized to what is a restriction. And if it is specified by a non-independent specifier, it does not benefit much, especially according to us. So Ibn al-Hajib's permission of ending (in description and condition to only two) where he said: by exception and substitution it is permissible to one, by the connected like description it is permissible to two, and by the disconnected in the limited few it is permissible to two, and in the unlimited to a number close to its meaning (is arbitrary). For the non-independent restrictions are all the same. Also, it is permissible for the described to be restricted by a description to a single individual, as indicated by undisputed induction, and denial is obstinacy, so understand. (And) for us (secondly) is His statement: 'Those to whom the people said: Indeed the people have gathered against you' [Al Imran 173] meaning for your fight. (And what is meant) by 'the people' the first (is Nu'aym ibn Mas'ud by agreement of the commentators, so the general term was intended for one, so that is the limit of specification. (The answer) as in Sharh al-Mukhtasar and others: that 'the people' is for the known (al-ma'hood), so it has no generality, hence no specification, so the claim is not established. (It is refuted) by saying: specification is like 'ahd' (knownness), for we require concurrency (muqarana) in the specifier, so the specified general term intended some of its individuals by the indication of a concurrent matter, similarly in 'ahd' some of what the form covers is intended by the indication of the concurrent 'lam'. It is rejected: undoubtedly 'ahd' is not truly general, so it cannot be claimed that intending some in 'ahd' is a type of specification of a general term. There remains only an analogy of specification to intending some in 'ahd', which is a linguistic analogy, so not valid. Know that repelling this question is easy: for whoever requires that 'ahd' have a previous mention, there is no previous mention of Nu'aym, nor was he known to the addressees so that their knowledge would substitute for mention, so there is no 'ahd'. And when [the condition] is not met, generality is determined as passed. But there is doubt about Nu'aym being intended, and the claim of agreement is rejected and not accepted. How? Ibn Ishaq and al-Bayhaqi narrated from Abdullah ibn Abi Bakr... [the story about the battle of Hamra al-Asad]. So the clearest evidence is that the relationship of metaphor is realized between the one and the whole, and hearing of particulars is not a condition for the validity of figurative usage. Hence it is permissible to use the general term for one, just as it is used for other ranks included in it. And there is no prohibition from language, and whoever claims it must provide proof. The majority (said): If someone says 'I killed everyone in the city' while in fact he killed three, it is considered nonsense. (We say) the nonsense is not conceded, except when no specifier is mentioned. Then specification is not permissible at all, not to three nor to most. And (when the specifier is mentioned with it) indicating that the intended is three, (we deny the entailment) of its being nonsense. If you say: how is it not considered nonsense when the speech has fallen below the level of eloquence? He said: (As for the fall of speech below eloquence, the discussion is not about that; rather the discussion is about linguistic correctness. Then the fall only occurs when the expression of the general term for three or one is without a rhetorical point. In that case, speech also falls if more remain when the expression lacks a point. But if there is a point, as when the three or one are such that the city's structure depends on them, and he killed them and said 'I killed all the city's people' elevating them to the status of the whole, then the fall is denied. And by what we have mentioned, what is said is refuted: that the purpose of the issue is to interpret the divine speech and prophetic hadith as specification to one or two; and since this would cause the speech to fall below eloquence, it cannot be applied to the two most eloquent speeches beyond which no human speech approaches. And if the respondent concedes the fall, then it follows that specification to three or less does not occur in the speech of the Lawgiver. So ponder. Those who permit to three or two (said): It is a restriction of the general term to some of the named, and the named (in the case of plural is three) for those who permit to three, (or two) for those who permit to two. If you say: this reasoning does not cover the desired case, for the general term may be other than plural. He said: (Perhaps they permitted specification (in non-plural to one). But this is not absolutely correct, for Shaykh Abu Bakr ibn al-Qaffal equated the forms of generality, whether plural or...
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the extent to which a general term ('amm) can be specified (takhsis). It is a dispute within Hanafi usul and against other schools. The text first presents the opinion of the majority that specification can go down to 'most' (more than half), but the author criticizes this as imprecise because the individuals of a general term are not limited. Other opinions: to three, to two, and the Hanafi choice is to one. The Hanafi proof is systematic: first, analogical reasoning that independent specifiers (like exception) and non-independent (like description) should be equal in effect, hence can reduce to one. But the author notes this depends on an assumption. Second, a Quranic proof from Al Imran 173 where 'الناس' is claimed to mean one person, Nu'aym ibn Mas'ud, showing that a general term can be used for one. The text then presents a counterargument that 'الناس' there is for 'ahd' (known/definite), not general, hence no takhsis. The author refutes this by arguing that 'ahd' itself is a type of specification because it also restricts the reference, and the condition of previous mention is not satisfied here. A longer narrative about the battle of Hamra al-Asad is provided from Ibn Ishaq and al-Bayhaqi to show the context. The passage then addresses the objection that using a general term for few individuals makes speech ineloquent, arguing that this is not a linguistic correctness issue but a rhetorical one; if there is a narrative purpose, it is not ineloquent. Finally, it mentions that some scholars permit specification to three or two based on the nature of plural, but this is rebutted by noting that general terms are not limited to plurals.

Key Terms
التخصيص (al-takhsis): Limiting a general term ('amm) to some of its individuals by a specifier (mukhasisis).
العام (al-'amm): A term that encompasses all individuals falling under it without limit.
المخصوص (al-mukhasisis): The specifier that limits the general term; can be independent (like exception) or connected (like description).
المعهود (al-ma'hood): The definite/known referent indicated by the definite article 'al-' when it refers to a previously mentioned or known entity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, to how many individuals can a general term ('amm) be specified?
A) To the most (more than half)
B) To three
C) To two
D) To one

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi madhhab permits specification of a general term to a single individual, supported by the Quranic verse Al Imran 173, where 'الناس' refers to one person, and no linguistic prohibition exists.

Module 6 · Lesson 172
