البعض، فللمثال المذكور إقرار بعشرة منقوص عنها ما يعبر عنه بثمانية منقوص عنها سبعة، وهو الواحد، فيبقى من العشرة بعد نقصانه تسعة، فهو مقر به، لأنه به التكلم وليس في المستثنى حكم فتأمل وربما يقال : الحنفية المنكرون للحكم في المستثنى ينكرونه مطلقاً عرفاً ولغة، فالتوجيه بإقرار الحكم المستثنى عرفاً، وإنكاره لغة توجيه بما لا يرضون به فافهم الحنفية الجاعلون للمستثنى في حكم المسكوت (قالوا: أولاً : نقل عن أهل العربية أنه تكلم بالباقي بعد الثنيا) فليس فيه تكلم بالمستثنى لا نفياً ولا إثباتاً (أقول) في الجواب : لا ينافي هذا النقل (ذلك النقل) وهو من الإثبات نفي ومن النفي إثبات فإن هذا باعتبار المستثنى منه أي ليس تكلماً بكل ما يتناول المستثنى منه بل بالباقي فقط (وأما الاقتصار على حكم الصدر فقط فلا نص فيه بل ساكت عنه بخلاف ذلك النقل، فإنه نص على مخالفة حكم المستثنى بحيث لا يقبل التأويل، وربما يجاب بأن المعنى أنه صريحاً تكلم بالباقي، وهذا لا ينافي تضمنه حكماً مخالفاً للصدر في المستثنى ومن ههنا أي من أجل أن هذا حكم المستثنى منه علم اندفاع ما قيل) في حواشي مرزاجان على شرح المختصر أن القول بالحكمين المتخالفين في المستثنى منه والمستثنى (لا يتأتى مع اختيار أن الإسناد بعد الإخراج وجه الاندفاع أن هذا حال المستثنى منه، فإن الإسناد إليه بعد الإخراج، وهذا لا ينافي في إفادته الحكم المخالف في المستثنى (فتدبر) وبه اندفع أيضاً في التوضيح أن الأليق بهذا المذهب أن لا يدل المستثنى على الحكم المخالف (و) قالوا (ثانياً : لو كان في المستثنى حكم اللزم من لا صلاة إلا بطهور صحتها بمجرد الطهور) لإفادة الاستثناء مخالف الصدر (وهو باطل اتفاقاً فإن الصلاة مع فقدان شروط أخرى من الستر ونحوه، وإن كانت مع الطهارة باطلة قطعاً، وما في بعض شروح المنهاج من أن الحديث المذكور غير صحيح غير واف فإنه وإن لم تكن الألفاظ صحيحة، لكن الحديث بلفظ : «لا يقبل الله الصلاة إلا بطهور صحيح بل ادعى السيوطي ،تواتره وقد ذكر في رسالة مفردة أسانيد كثيرة له فافهم (ويجاب أوّلاً كما أقول بأن (البطلان في بعض الصور مع وجود الطهارة لمعارضة) دليل قاطع دل على اشتراط أمر آخر من الاستقبال والستر وغير ذلك (لا يضر) مدعانا (فإنه مخصص) لعموم حكم الاستثناء، وإنما يضر لو ادعينا الأحكام وعدم قبول التخصيص، بل الدعوى الظهور وإن قبل التخصيص ،ونحوه، غاية ما في الباب أنه ظاهر في ثبوت الصحة مع فقدان سائر الشروط لولا المعارض القاطع (فافهم) وقد يقال لا بد للمخصص من المقارنة ولا مقارنة ههنا ولا احتمال للنسخ ههنا وهو غير واف، فإن اشتراط الشروط الأخر من ضروريات الدين وكان متقدماً عليه فيصلح مخصصاً، وإنما لا يصلح للتخصيص ما يظهر بعد ورود العام فافهم (و) يجاب (ثانياً كما قال الآمدي إنه منقطع فلا إخراج) فيه لشيء من أفراد الصلاة بل فيه حكم (آخر) من ثبوت الصحة مع الطهارة ولو في بعض الأحيان (ويدفع) هذا الجواب بأنه (مفرغ) لأن المعنى لا صلاة حاصلة ملتصقة بشيء إلا ملتصقة بطهور (وكل مفرغ متصل كما تقرر في النحو، وقد يقال : كونه مفرغاً غير متعين، إذ يجوز أن يكون التقدير هكذا : لا صلاة موجودة إلا صلاة بطهور ، فالمستثنى منه هو الصلاة، فالوجه في الدفع أن يقال :أولاً : إن الانقطاع يفيد عدم صحة الصلاة عموماً، لكن قد تكون مقرونة بطهارة، وثانياً : إن الاتصال ممكن بل متبادر وظاهر، فلا يعدل إلى الانقطاع الذي يصار إليه بضرورة شديدة (و) يجاب (ثالثاً كما في «المنهاج بحمله على (المبالغة في اشتراط الطهارة (كأنه لا شرط للصحة غيرها) فلا يلزم الصحة مع فقدان سائر الشروط ولا يخفى أنه أي الحمل على المبالغة (خلاف الأصل سيما في الشرع فلا يصار إليه، كيف ولو فتح هذا الباب لما ثبت حكم أصلاً (و) يجاب (رابعاً) كما في المختصر أن قدر خبر مستثنى منه وقيل (لا صلاة)
It does not contradict the placement for meanings in themselves, for it is placed for exclusion in itself, and not addressing likewise, so reflect. The truth in the answer is that the transmitted report cannot bear this interpretation, for they stated that it is from negation affirmation of what is negated, and vice versa, and this contradicts not addressing. And it was answered regarding the objection to the second proof that the custom of the Lawgiver is recent, and the discussion is about the word of tawhid before its occurrence in early Islam when addressing the disbelievers with it, for they understood from it tawhid without knowledge of the Law and its custom. Unless it is said in repelling this answer that the addressee at that time was not a deist denying the existence of God, but rather was a polytheist, as God said: 'And if you ask them who created the heavens and the earth, they will surely say Allah.' And if he was not a deist, the existence of God was acknowledged by him, so he was not addressed with affirming and acknowledging it because they were already present. Then tawhid became thereafter a custom of the Lawgiver. And a second objection was raised against them: the dispute concerns linguistic indication: according to them it does not indicate linguistically the opposite, whereas according to the majority it does indicate linguistically. The aforementioned transmitted report is interpreted as their being established customarily, and they have no argument about it; indeed they have stated it. Thus it necessitates seven according to them in examples like 'I have nothing except seven,' and if it were not customary for establishing seven, it would not be necessitated. And tawhid is also completed because it conveys customarily negation and affirmation. By this is repelled what was said that denying the indication of 'ma qama illa Zayd' for the establishment of standing for Zayd, as is their view of no indication for affirmation and negation, nearly approaches denial of necessities. The repelling point is that the necessary extent is the indication customarily, and they do not deny it; they only deny the indication by placement. Thus what is denied is not necessary, and what is necessary is not denied. I say in refuting the answer secondly: This allowance, despite its remoteness in itself, for there is no evidence for language except transmission from its people, and since you have interpreted the transmission as custom, then let it be applied to every transmission, so no word is established by placement, and this is sophistry. For the linguists only reported the linguistic placement, and it is not valid to interpret it as explaining custom. It entails that exception from exception is valid linguistically, for exception requires a ruling in the first part, and since there is no ruling linguistically in exception, then exception from it is not valid, like 'I have ten except eight except seven,' and it is valid according to the soundest school. So reflect, for the respondent can deny the validity of exception from exception linguistically; indeed since he denied the ruling in it linguistically, this validity is even more unlikely. This is concessively, otherwise he can deny that exception requires a prior ruling. How? For the ruling after exclusion is on what is called the qualified; it is possible to consider the excepted as qualified by the exclusion of some, then qualify the excepted-from by the exclusion of this qualified excepted, then rule on what is true of this composite qualification, i.e., the general diminished by the excepted diminished by some. So for the mentioned example, there is an acknowledgment of ten diminished by what is expressed as eight diminished by seven, which is one, so what remains from ten after its diminution is nine, so it is acknowledged by him because he spoke of it, and there is no ruling in the excepted. So ponder. And perhaps it is said: The Hanafis who deny the ruling in the excepted deny it absolutely both customarily and linguistically, so the interpretation of acknowledging the ruling in the excepted customarily while denying it linguistically is an interpretation they would not accept. So understand: The Hanafis who make the excepted like the unmentioned said: First: It is transmitted from Arabic scholars that he spoke of the remainder after the exception. So he did not speak of the excepted, neither negatively nor affirmatively. I say in response: This transmission does not contradict that transmission, which is from affirmation negation and from negation affirmation, for this is with respect to the excepted-from, i.e., he did not speak of everything that the excepted-from encompasses but only the remainder. As for restricting to the ruling of the first part only, there is no text for it but rather silence, unlike that transmission, for it states the opposite ruling of the excepted such that it does not admit interpretation. And perhaps it is answered that the meaning is that he explicitly spoke of the remainder, and this does not contradict its containing a ruling opposed to the first part for the excepted. And from here, i.e., because this is the ruling of the excepted-from, it is known that what was said in the marginalia of Mirzajan on the commentary of al-Mukhtasar that the view of two differing rulings in the excepted-from and the excepted is not possible together with the choice that the attribution is after exclusion. The repelling point is that this is the case of the excepted-from, for the attribution to it is after exclusion, and this does not contradict its imparting the opposite ruling in the excepted. So reflect. And by this is also repelled what is in al-Tawdih that the more fitting with this school is that the excepted does not indicate the opposite ruling. And they said secondly: If there were a ruling in the excepted, then from 'No prayer except with purification' it would necessitate its validity merely by purification because the exception imparts the opposite of the first part, and this is unanimously invalid. For prayer with the loss of other conditions like covering etc., even if it is with purification, is absolutely invalid. And what is in some commentaries of al-Minhaj that the aforementioned hadith is not authentic is insufficient, for even if the words are not authentic, the hadith in the wording 'Allah does not accept prayer except with purification' is authentic; indeed al-Suyuti claimed its tawatur, and he mentioned many chains for it in a separate treatise. So understand. And it is answered firstly as I say: The invalidity in some cases despite the presence of purification is due to a definitive evidence that indicates the stipulation of another condition like facing the qibla, covering, etc., and does not harm our claim, for it specifies the general meaning of the exception. It would only harm if we claimed absolute rulings and no acceptance of specification; rather the claim is merely apparent, even if it accepts specification and the like. The upshot of the matter is that it is apparent in establishing validity with the loss of other conditions were it not for the definitive contradicting evidence. So understand. And it may be said: The specifying evidence must be contemporaneous, and there is no contemporaneity here, nor any possibility of abrogation here, and this is insufficient, for the stipulation of the other conditions is from the necessities of religion and was prior to it, so it can serve as a specifier. Only what appears after the occurrence of the general cannot serve as specification. So understand. And it is answered secondly as al-Amidi said: It is discontinuous (munqati'), so there is no exclusion of any individual of prayer, rather there is another ruling: the establishment of validity with purification even if in some instances. And this answer is repelled by saying it is continuous (mufarrag) because the meaning is: There is no prayer occurring attached to something except attached to purification, and every continuous construction (mufarrag) is connected as established in grammar. And it may be said: Its being mufarrag is not certain, for it is possible that the estimation is thus: There is no existing prayer except prayer with purification, so the excepted-from is prayer. So the repelling point is to say: First, discontinuity implies the invalidity of prayer in general, but it may be accompanied with purification, and second, connection is possible, indeed immediately understood and apparent, so one does not resort to discontinuity which is only used under extreme necessity. And it is answered thirdly as in al-Minhaj by interpreting it as hyperbole in stipulating purification, as if there is no condition for validity besides it, so validity is not necessitated with the loss of other conditions. And it is not hidden that this interpretation of hyperbole is contrary to the principle, especially in the Law, so one does not resort to it. How? If this door were opened, no ruling would ever be established. And it is answered fourthly as in al-Mukhtasar that it is estimated as a predicate with an excepted-from, and it was said: 'No prayer.'
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage is a detailed usul al-fiqh dispute concerning the linguistic and customary indication of exception (istithna). The commentator is expanding on the matn of Musallam al-Thubut, defending the Hanafi position that exception does not, by itself, impart a legal ruling for the excepted item (mustathna); rather, it merely excludes the excepted from the general statement. The Hanafis argue that the excepted is like the unmentioned (maskut anhu) — it carries no independent ruling. The passage begins by addressing an objection: the claim that the word of tawhid (la ilaha illa Allah) is not contradictory because it is placed for meanings in themselves. The Hanafi response is that the transmitted evidence about exception indicating the opposite is not applicable here because the custom of the Lawgiver (urf al-shari) emerged later; the early polytheists already affirmed God's existence, so they were not commanded to affirm it anew. The debate then shifts to linguistic vs. customary indication. The Hanafis maintain that exception does not indicate the opposite linguistically, but the majority (including Shafi'is) argue it does. The commentator rebuts the majority's reliance on transmitted reports by showing that if those reports are interpreted as custom, then no linguistic placement can be proven, leading to skepticism. He also tackles the issue of exception from exception, showing that the Hanafi view is consistent. The second major argument is from the hadith 'La salata illa bi-tahur' (No prayer except with purification). If exception implied the opposite, then any prayer with purification would be valid, but that is false because other conditions are needed. The Hanafis respond with specification (takhsis): the hadith is general regarding purification but specified by other definitive texts requiring facing qibla, covering, etc. Alternative responses include interpreting the hadith as discontinuous (munqati') or as hyperbole, but these are rejected because connection is the default and hyperbole is contrary to legal principles. The commentator concludes by noting the complexity and urging careful reflection ('fatadabbara'). The entire discussion illustrates the Hanafi commitment to a strict reading of linguistic indication and the avoidance of unnecessary implications from exception.

Key Terms
الاستثناء (al-istithna): A linguistic construct that excludes something from a general statement; according to Hanafis, it does not itself impart a ruling for the excepted.
المستثنى (al-mustathna): The item excluded by the exception; in Hanafi usul, it is treated like the unmentioned (maskut anhu) with no independent ruling.
المنقطع (al-munqati'): A type of exception where the excepted is not from the same genus as the excepted-from (e.g., 'I have ten except a camel'); here used as an interpretation of the hadith.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position discussed in this passage, what is the ruling on the excepted item (mustathna) in a statement like 'Ma qama illa Zayd'?
A) The excepted (Zayd) is affirmed to have stood linguistically.
B) The excepted has no ruling; it is like the unmentioned.
C) The excepted is negated, meaning Zayd did not stand.
D) The excepted is affirmed customarily but not linguistically.

Key Takeaway
Exception (istithna) does not by itself impart a ruling for the excepted; the excepted is like the unmentioned according to the Hanafi school.
